Factory Worker Who Committed Suicide" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/c0f958011c7161670d6349f9f5e206757db33233.jpg"><em>(BGR)</em></p>  <p>Foxconn, the Chinese manufacturing giant where the world&#x2019;s iPhones are assembled, has a <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/01/26/business/ieconomy-apples-ipad-and-the-human-costs-for-workers-in-china.html" target="_blank">reputation</a> for poor working conditions. Now a <a href="https://libcom.org/blog/xulizhi-foxconn-suicide-poetry" target="_blank">trove of translated poetry</a> from a factory worker who committed suicide shines new light into the devastating emotional and physical toll of that job.</p>  <p><span>Xu Lizhi first began working in the assembly line at Foxconn&#x2019;s Shenzen facility in 2010. During his employment, he published nearly 30 pieces in the company&#x2019;s internal newspaper, &#x201C;Foxconn People,&#x201D; including poems describing the plant&#x2019;s poor working conditions. </span></p>  <p><span>Lizhi killed himself in September 2014 at the age of 24. In late October, the <a href="https://libcom.org/blog/xulizhi-foxconn-suicide-poetry" target="_blank">N&#xE0;o Project</a> &#x2014; a multilingual blog and journal dedicated to human rights &#x2014; <a href="http://www.businessinsider.com/foxconn-factory-workers-suicide-poems-2014-11" target="_blank">translated his obituary and poems</a> to &#x201C;<span>spread awareness [of] the harsh conditions, struggles and aspirations of Chinese migrant workers.&#x201D;</span></span></p>  <p><img alt="Obituary in Shenzen Evening News" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w432/fe64804e8579b9f56da20cf8cbbf27891f6fb0df.png"><br><em>A screenshot of Lizhi&#x2019;s obituary, which ran in his hometown paper, the&#xA0;<a href="http://wb.sznews.com/html/2014-10/10/content_3025410.htm" target="_blank">Shenzhen Evening News</a>.</em></p>  <p><span></span></p>  <p><span>The titles of Lizhi&#x2019;s work include&#xA0;</span><span>&#x201C;I Fall Asleep, Just Standing Like That&#x201D; and &#x201C;The Last Graveyard.&#x201D; They depict a joyless, almost robotic existence full of overnight shifts, docile suffering, and a toxic working environment.</span></p>  <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>One of Lizhi&#x2019;s shorter works from January 2014,&#xA0;<span>&#x201C;A Screw Fell to the Ground,&#x201D;</span> hints at the company&#x2019;s lack of concern for exhausted employees.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>  <p><em>A screw fell to the ground<br></em><em>In this dark night of overtime<br></em><em>Plunging vertically, lightly clinking<br></em><em>It won&#x2019;t attract anyone&#x2019;s attention<br></em><em>Just like last time<br></em><em>On a night like this<br></em><em>When someone plunged to the ground</em></p>  <p>News of Foxconn&#x2019;s inhumane conditions spread to international circles as early as 2010, the year that 18 Foxconn workers separately <a href="http://www.reuters.com/article/2010/11/05/us-china-foxconn-death-idUSTRE6A41M920101105" target="_blank">attempted suicide</a> by leaping off a structure at the manufacturing facility. Fourteen died. The pattern <a href="http://online.wsj.com/news/articles/SB10001424052748704026204575267603576594936?mg=reno64-wsj&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fonline.wsj.com%2Farticle%2FSB10001424052748704026204575267603576594936.html" target="_blank">sparked inquiries</a> from some of Foxconn&#x2019;s customers, including Apple and Hewlett-Packard.</p>  <p>By 2012, <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/12/27/business/signs-of-changes-taking-hold-in-electronics-factories-in-china.html" target="_blank">The New York Times</a> reported that Foxconn had improved its conditions, after company executives sat down with Apple officials and negotiated changes. Employees were given chairs to sit on (which previously were considered incentives for laziness), as well as more substantial improvements such as shorter shifts and higher pay.</p>  <p><span>But the fact that these disturbing poems appeared in an internal factory newspaper &#x2014; and that not one Foxconn supervisor, administrator, or executive expressed concern for Lizhi or his co-workers &#x2014; is a telling sign that the company is far from resolving the problems that have plagued it in the past.</span></p>  <p><em>Follow <a href="https://twitter.com/alyssabereznak" target="_blank">Alyssa Bereznak on Twitter</a> or <a href="mailto:alyssab@yahoo-inc.com" target="_blank">email her</a>.</em></p></div><div class="post-cut" data-reactid=".21cpxzdcrnk.0.0.0.$Pos-r.$article-inner-container.$inset-container.$grid-template.0.$col-left.$content.$grid-content.0.1.$text-body.0.1"></div></div></div><div class="comments-applet" riginal\u002FXkdRbsxrbEnpnndgBTYvrPEcOJs"}],"highlight_color":"#ffffff","data_version":"1","title":"Why WireLurker, the iPhone’s Most Advanced Malware Ever, Shouldn’t Terrify You","summary":"You may have heard that a new strain of malware called WireLurker has attacked Apple’s OS X operating system for Mac and iOS devices like the iPhone and iPad. Don't be afraid.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Why WireLurker, the iPhone&#x2019;s Most Advanced Malware Ever, Shouldn&#x2019;t Terrify You\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F2a64fa1a754560b6fa554d5e045ed9ec6a69a87b.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYou may have heard that a new strain of malware called \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fs\u002Fmost-advanced-iphone-malware-yet-terrify-133038080.html\"\u003EWireLurker\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has attacked Apple&#x2019;s OS&#xA0;X operating system for Mac and iOS devices like the iPhone and iPad. You might have also heard that it&#x2019;s incredibly dangerous and that you should be very, very scared.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut the truth is, the malware itself has already been addressed and subdued by Apple. It also was never that big of a threat to most people, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbgr.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002F06\u002Fiphone-and-mac-malware-wirelurker\u002F\"\u003Edespite what you may have read elsewhere\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The real issue, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.paloaltonetworks.com\u002Fcompany\u002Fpress\u002F2014\u002Fpalo-alto-networks-reveals-discovery-of-unprecedented-ios-and-os-x-malware.html\"\u003Eaccording to Palo Alto Networks\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the security company that found the malware, is how it infected your iPhone, and what that could mean for \u003Cem\u003Efuture\u003C\u002Fem\u003E attacks.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMembers of Palo Alto Network&#x2019;s Unit 42 uncovered WireLurker earlier this week. This piece of malware, which may have been downloaded hundreds of thousands of times, required you to take very specific actions for it to get onto your iPhone.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EFirst of all, you had to go to a third-party Chinese OS&#xA0;X app store called the Maiyadi App Store &#x2014; a dangerous Web store known to host pirated and infected OS&#xA0;X software. You then had to ignore a host of warnings from OS&#xA0;X asking whether you really wanted to run software from an unknown developer or source.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThose steps alone mean that the vast majority of OS&#xA0;X and iPhone owners were safe from WireLurker from the start. You&#x2019;re probably not downloading too much software from third-party Chinese app stores. (And if you are: Stop it.)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EEven if you are frequenting the Maiyadi App Store, it would take another step for this malware to get onto your iPhone: You would have had to plug your phone into your infected Mac via USB. WireLurker would then jump to your iPhone and start mining data. \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWhat the ultimate purpose of the malware was has yet to be uncovered. But, needless to say, o\u003C\u002Fspan\u003Enly a small minority of people were ever in danger of seeing their devices infected by WireLurker.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe thing that makes WireLurker a problem, and the reason it deserves so much attention, is that it was able to impact iPhones that weren&#x2019;t &#x201C;jailbroken.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EJailbreaking an iPhone basically gives a person the ability to install and run apps and extensions that Apple&#x2019;s iOS normally doesn&#x2019;t allow for a variety of reasons, including security. Jailbreaking is also popular for those who want to use a device on their local carrier, which may or may not support Apple devices.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EJailbreaking is capable of enabling a lot of cool stuff on your phone that Apple otherwise blocks. The problem with jailbreaking an iPhone is that, if you&#x2019;re not careful, it can put your phone at risk of being infected by malware or other malicious software.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMalware on jailbroken iPhones, in other words, isn&#x2019;t new. WireLurker, however, managed to infect iPhones that hadn&#x2019;t been jailbroken. It did so by exploiting enterprise provisions within Apple&#x2019;s iOS, which are normally used by businesses to create custom apps for their employees.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThat&#x2019;s the reason WireLurker is dangerous. It&#x2019;s not some super piece of malware that will destroy your iPhone, as it&#x2019;s been made out to be. The scary thing is the means by which it was able to install itself on non-jailbroken iPhones.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EAccording to Palo Alto Networks, WireLurker is only the third piece of malware that&#x2019;s managed to infect non-jailbroken iPhones. What&#x2019;s more, this is one of the first instances of malicious software being able to jump to non-jailbroken iPhones via a USB connection. \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn other words, this likely won&#x2019;t be the last type of malware that attacks iPhones in such a way. Where the next attack will come from is one of those pesky known unknowns.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ESo how do you keep your iPhone safe from such an attack? Just follow the usual rules for device safety. Don&#x2019;t download software from places you don&#x2019;t know you can trust, install an antivirus suite on your Mac, keep your Mac and iPhone up to date, and don&#x2019;t jailbreak your iPhone if you aren&#x2019;t sure how to avoid malware. If you do all that, you&#x2019;re likely safe.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ENow stop panicking and get back to taking selfies, or playing Flappy Crush Saga, Halo’s a universe full of mysteries, though.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"10 Things You Might Not Know About &#x2018;Halo&#x2019;\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F4cb24c2e0f92a5186d572f531967f78507d7f449.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMaster Chief has been a pretty busy Spartan since blasting onto the Xbox in 2001.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHe&#x2019;s saved the universe a few times, spawned a New York Times best-selling series of books, and has caught the eye of heavyweights like Ridley Scott and Steven Spielberg. Next up is the Nov. 11 release of \u003Cem\u003EHalo: The Master Chief Collection\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, a compilation of the four main \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E games along with a ton of extra goodies.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&#x2019;s a universe full of mysteries, though. As you get ready to step into Chief&#x2019;s extremely heavy boots, brush up on your \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E trivia.\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"280.95238095238096\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FTzrme9yWens\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E1. Steve Jobs debuted it.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMaster Chief has shilled for Microsoft for so long that it&#x2019;s easy to forget that, in the beginning, he was an equal opportunity fanboy.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn its early years, \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E maker Bungie developed games simultaneously for both Mac and PC. Apple CEO Steve Jobs was so taken by the work on \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E that he trotted the game out onstage during the 1999 MacWorld Expo &#x2014; the first time the game was shown publicly. \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EUnfortunately, his joy wouldn&#x2019;t last long. The following year, Microsoft bought Bungie, converted \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E into an Xbox launch title, and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.develop-online.net\u002Fnews\u002Fsteve-jobs-raged-at-microsoft-over-game-studio-sale\u002F0108013\"\u003Emade Jobs furious\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E2. It didn&#x2019;t start off as a shooter.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThese days \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E is synonymous with console first-person shooters, but it didn&#x2019;t start out as one.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBefore the Xbox was in the picture, Bungie had envisioned \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E as a real-time strategy game. It later moved into the action genre, becoming a third-person cooperative game (complete with a flamethrower and spear gun) before evolving into the \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E we know today. \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=7Tqrfy4SR7I\"\u003EWant to see the pre-Xbox build?\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" title=\"BBC news report featuring logo from Halo\" width=\"630\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F0d1a5bdb67b19086ee09bee6afc0ffbd67398a17.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E3. It&#x2019;s been confused with the U.N.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ERunning a 24-hour news desk can&#x2019;t be easy, but the fact checkers for the BBC blew it big-time in 2012 during a story about Syria.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhile discussing actions taken by the United Nations Security Council, the network \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.eurogamer.net\u002Farticles\u002F2012-05-28-bbc-news-mistakes-halo-unsc-logo-for-un\"\u003Eaccidentally used a logo for a different UNSC\u003C\u002Fa\u003E &#x2014; the United Nations Space Command from \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. To be fair, a few Spartan soldiers would make pretty good peacekeepers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E4. The UNSC is full of Real American Heroes\u003Cspan\u003E&#x2122;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EOne of the first voices you hear in \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo: Combat Evolved\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E should sound familiar if you&#x2019;ve listened to the radio since the late 1990s. Captain Jacob Keyes of the UNSC is voiced by Pete Stacker, whose ridiculous readings of Budweiser&#x2019;s \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbudlight.whipnet.com\u002F\"\u003EReal American Heroes\u002FReal Men of Genius commercials\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E made them so successful that the beer company eventually released a CD of the ads.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E5. Cortana and Princess Peach are BFFs.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E&#x2019;s helpful Cortana and Nintendo&#x2019;s perpetually kidnapped Princess Peach aren&#x2019;t much alike, which makes it all the more impressive that the same person voices the two characters.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ENot only does Jen Taylor give voice to Master Chief&#x2019;s digital pal, but Microsoft loved her so much in the role that it brought her on to do the voice of the digital assistant for Windows Phone, too.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" title=\"Steve Downes\" width=\"630\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F97ae1aa7d27dff2670e72594a95eebb38323ebe1.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E6. Master Chief is also a DJ.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe hero of \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E isn&#x2019;t particularly social. He&#x2019;s a man of few words, his best friend is a computer A.I., and he spends most of his time wandering around alone. So it&#x2019;s especially hard to picture him grooving to \u003Cspan\u003ECreedence&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EClearwater Revival.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut Steve Downes digs some CCR, that&#x2019;s for sure. The man who gives Master Chief his voice is \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgames.yahoo.com\u002Fblogs\u002Fplugged-in\u002Fmeet-man-behind-master-chief-183609474.html\"\u003E\u003Cspan\u003Ea DJ on WDRV (&#x201C;The Drive&#x201D;) in Chicago\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Downes was one of several Chicago-area voice actors Bungie hired when it began casting the original \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. He took the job but didn&#x2019;t give it much thought until he was visiting a friend in Florida and kids swarmed him, Flood-like, for an autograph.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E7. He&#x2019;s also old enough to be your father (maybe).\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EHe&#x2019;s strong enough to wander the universe in a 1,000-pound suit, but according to \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E lore, Master Chief is no spring chicken. Having started out fighting the Covenant when he was only 14, Chief is now well into his 40s. Watch your back, Chief. Seriously, watch it. Use your core.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"280.95238095238096\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FuHRKHNZLebY\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E8. Its music owes a debt to Fred and Wilma.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMarty O&#x2019;Donnell&#x2019;s soundtrack is as much a part of the \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E franchise as Master Chief. But before he crossed paths with Bungie (a relationship that \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.polygon.com\u002F2014\u002F4\u002F16\u002F5619696\u002Fbungie-terminates-halo-series-composer-marty-odonnell\"\u003Eended badly\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E earlier this year), O&#x2019;Donnell was in the advertising business, writing jingles for commercials &#x2014; including the \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003Eiconic one \u003Cspan\u003Efor Flintstones vitamins&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003Ein the above video\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E. Sorry that&#x2019;s stuck in your head now.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E9. \u003Cem\u003EHalo 2\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&#x2019;s soundtrack is a wonderland.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn addition to O&#x2019;Donnell, a few big names contributed to the music of \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo 2\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E. Famed songwriter Nile Rodgers took the lead as producer, bringing in the likes of legendary guitarist Steve Vai to lay down some tracks.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut O&#x2019;Donnell \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=W9-Wk_R3SPw#t=1028\"\u003Erecently revealed\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that another guitarist, John Mayer, contributed to two tracks as well, entirely off the books. A huge \u003Cem\u003EHalo\u003C\u002Fem\u003E fan, Mayer apparently just wanted to be able to tell his friends that he was on the soundtrack to \u003Cem\u003EHalo 2.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E10. It&#x2019;s a political distraction.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIt&#x2019;s common for gamers to call in sick the day a big game releases, but in the case of \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo 4\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, it didn&#x2019;t just upset employers &#x2014; it upset political activists, too.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EHalo 4\u003C\u002Fem\u003E was released on Nov. 6, 2012 &#x2014; the same day voters headed to the polls to hand the keys to the White House to Barack Obama or Mitt Romney. Some \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgames.yahoo.com\u002Fblogs\u002Fplugged-in\u002Factivists-halo-4-may-affect-presidential-race-184916930.html\"\u003E\u003Cspan\u003Efeared the excitement\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E over the game would keep younger voters away. 0","data_version":"1","title":"HTC Re Camera Review: An Inhaler-Shaped Camera That Misses the Mark","summary":"A $199 mini camera, the oddly shaped Re is meant to keep you “in the moment” by eliminating the most distracting part of a camera, the viewfinder.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re Camera Review: An Inhaler-Shaped Camera That Misses the Mark\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fd7ded3b0e74c67dba4ba6691eca05ae63e520385.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWe spend so much time behind the camera viewfinders on our smartphones that we no longer \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003Etruly \u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003Esee our subjects or the world around us. That&#x2019;s the idea behind HTC&#x2019;s weird new Re Camera.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EA $199 mini camera, the oddly shaped Re is meant to keep you &#x201C;in the moment&#x201D; instead of gawking at a viewfinder. How does the company accomplish this goal? By simply removing the viewfinder from the equation, that&#x2019;s how.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThat&#x2019;s right: The Re is a camera that lets you take pictures without knowing how they&#x2019;ll turn out. Keeping you in the moment while taking photos is an intriguing idea &#x2014; comedian Louis C.K. touched on a similar thought during one of his \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbuy.louisck.net\u002Fpurchase\u002Foh-my-god\"\u003Estandup acts\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EUnfortunately, its price and photo quality leave much to be desired.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EIt looks like a periscope\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Re certainly looks interesting. It reminds me of the one-eyed garbage monster from \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EStar Wars\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E. Or, you know, a submarine&#x2019;s periscope. Or an inhaler.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re mini-camera with plastic toys\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Ff1996ae742df12b38f7059eda894690f26686aae.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe 2.3-ounce camera is surprisingly comfortable to hold thanks to its unique design. It also, as my colleague Alyssa Bereznak observed, happens to look like a detonator a James Bond villain would use to blow up a bridge.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Re is extremely functional, though, as the front portion where you rest your fingers features a sensor that detects when you&#x2019;re holding the camera and prepares it to take a picture. No more having to open and wait for your camera app to load. Just pick up the Re and start shooting photos.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re mini-camera in a hand\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fa825707343916524effadf532ffe09d17ee2c9a3.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EUp front, the Re gets a 146-degree wide-angle lens that can take either standard or warped, fisheye-style photos. You can adjust how your photos look in the Re smartphone app, but I&#x2019;ll get to that in a second.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EBecause it&#x2019;s made of plastic, the Re can&#x2019;t be tortured like, say, a GoPro can, but it can withstand being submerged in up to 3 feet of water for 30 minutes without issue.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Re is not dust- or sand-proof, though. Taking it to the beach is basically out of the question.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EUsing the Re\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EOK, so it&#x2019;s shaped weirdly and you can&#x2019;t see what you&#x2019;re taking pictures of. Here&#x2019;s what it&#x2019;s like to use.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re mini-camera in a hand\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F453285e1ee04745370c704b6d9ebeac66935db32.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIt&#x2019;s a mixed bag of nuts. Taking pictures is incredibly easy thanks to the Re&#x2019;s giant shutter button, but when I looked at a lot of the pictures I took, they were all lopsided since I wasn&#x2019;t used to using a camera without a viewfinder.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Crooked photo of New York City street\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F1aac8b3c02378eba9bbca22476d75aec6805d13e.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIf you really need to see what you&#x2019;re taking pictures of, you can download the Re app for Android and iOS. The app serves as both a means to view all your pictures taken with the Re and gives you the ability to use your phone&#x2019;s screen as a viewfinder.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re camera app\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Ff34a4d9914464622ec425a61718b2fce84e4c75c.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EJust point the Re at anything you want, and it will show up on your phone&#x2019;s screen. You can even control the camera&#x2019;s shutter from your handset, so you can take pictures from across the room.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe app also lets you adjust camera settings including photo and video resolution, switch between wide-angle and standard shooting modes, turn on video stabilization, and add location data to your photos.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re camera app\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F6ce75aad38453e2e334e7f6a0113b495841f25d2.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe app is helpful for situations like taking group photos or, in my case, taking pictures of an incredibly camera-shy dog. I also like that it gives me a means to see all my pictures stored on the camera itself, without having to download them to my computer or phone.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPhoto quality\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Re&#x2019;s 16-megapixel camera captured decently sharp pictures, as long as I was standing still. Despite its image-stabilization software, photos taken with the Re while I or my subject was moving were consistently blurry.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Blurry picture of dog\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Ff9de68fc21ebb3f4a7a19d9f2da3e2bc09273e46.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhen I stayed in one spot, though, my photos turned out relatively clear each time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re picture of dog\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F9c0975aff79bdaba426d0438add5460b1ca730ae.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EVideo, on the other hand, is always pixelated, even when taken at 1080p. Slow-motion video, which is automatically shot at 720p, is similarly grainy. \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fif-you-ask-most-people-what-a-polaroid-camera-is-98472975924.html\"\u003EPolaroid&#x2019;s $99 Cube\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which also has no viewfinder, captures lower-quality stills but cleaner video.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Re&#x2019;s lack of a viewfinder led me to learn that I am naturally lopsided. It seemed like every time I took a picture or video, my photos were slanted toward one side or the other. Eventually I learned to pay more attention to how I was holding the Re, though, and my photos started to even out.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"HTC Re picture of dog\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F040cf790863ce885f868e1278c7f1564a85793a7.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EI&#x2019;ve got to hand it to HTC, however, for making a small camera with an impressive battery life. I took about 150 photos and a few videos, and this little guy&#x2019;s battery was still rocking.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EShould you buy it?\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Re camera is a cool concept that needs more development. Its grip sensor is ingenious. And the way the camera interfaces with your phone so you can see all your photos instantly is excellent.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EBut most people will have a hard time adjusting to taking pictures without knowing how they&#x2019;ll come out. Do you really want to risk having your photos turn out blurry without knowing you should retake them?\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ETo be honest, I really like the idea of a camera that keeps you &#x201C;in the moment&#x201D; rather than making you focus on a viewfinder. But at $199, the HTC Re is too expensive. If you&#x2019;re interested in an on-the-go camera like the Re, check out the $99 Polaroid Cube. Animals Hanging Out with Robots: A Brief History","summary":"Robots \u003C3 animals, and animals \u003C3 robots.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Adorable Animals Hanging Out with Robots: A Brief History\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F74cdc3c6d0e2498bb69836768250699e56580ec1.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(Frederique Olivier\u002FDowner Productions)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIf you&#x2019;re the kind of person who can&#x2019;t resist a serious-sounding story made palatable by a huge dose of adorable, then surely you caught the robot-penguin news this week.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe serious part: a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nature.com\u002Fnmeth\u002Fjournal\u002Fvaop\u002Fncurrent\u002Ffull\u002Fnmeth.3173.html#close\"\u003Estudy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E looking into new ways to conduct scientific observations of penguins and seals in the wild &#x2014; minimizing the disturbance caused by human observers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe adorable part: basically a little remote-controlled vehicle adorned with what looks like a baby-penguin plush toy.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis &#x201C;penguin-bot,&#x201D; as \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fio9.com\u002Fthis-adorable-robotic-penguin-is-changing-the-way-we-st-1654021462\"\u003Eio9 dubbed it\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, was surprisingly successful at mingling with actual penguins. In fact, at one almost intolerably cute juncture, it was evidently mobbed by actual baby penguins.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"281.25\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002Fp_1vVtYqWxw\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EMotherboard\u003C\u002Fem\u003E writer Becky Ferreira puts this cutie-bot in the category of &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fread\u002Fwhy-secret-robot-agents-are-the-future-of-ecology\"\u003Ecamouflaged reconnaissance robots\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x201D; and notes a couple of previous examples.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe impressive result is summarized in this clip from the BBC, in which image-capturing devices made to look like fish and other aquatic creatures shot wonderful footage of dolphins that would have been unlikely to accept a human in their midst.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"281.25\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002F7w8FGVkEItQ?rel=0\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EFerreira also pointed out prior research involving waterborne, camera-equipped craft made to resemble crocodiles in order \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fread\u002Fhippo-poop-drones-test-water-quality\"\u003Eto study hippos\u003C\u002Fa\u003E &#x2014; which can be surprisingly dangerous. About \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fyoutu.be\u002FfamwtubAcBE?t=57s\"\u003Ea minute into this video\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, in fact, a hippo makes a run at one of the croco-bots. (Despite the shameless soundtrack, it all works out.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"281.25\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FfamwtubAcBE?rel=0\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPoking around a little more led me to wildlife photographer \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.burrard-lucas.com\u002F\"\u003EWill Burrard-Lucas&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;BeetleCam &#x2014; which is not disguised as an animal at all. Instead it&#x2019;s a sort of fortified, remote-controlled mini-buggy that gets a camera up close to lions and other wild animals without the documentarian risking her life. Evidently these photogenic beasts are more willing to put up with what looks like a rolling lunchbox than with \u003Cem\u003Ehomo sapiens. \u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBurrard-Lucas has made several versions of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.burrard-lucas.com\u002Fbeetlecam\"\u003Edevice\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in the past few years, the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fsingularityhub.com\u002F2014\u002F03\u002F26\u002Fwatch-how-robots-and-drones-are-transforming-wildlife-documentaries\u002F\"\u003Emore recent iterations\u003C\u002Fa\u003E equipped with both a still camera and a video-taking GoPro.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"281.25\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002Feu8gG1ioMjc?rel=0\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt turns out that at some level the idea of robots mingling with animals is just a modern update of a long-standing research practice.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Since the inception of the field of ethology,&#x201D; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.the-scientist.com\u002F?articles.view\u002FarticleNo\u002F37635\u002Ftitle\u002FSend-in-the-Bots\u002F\"\u003Ethis overview in The Scientist \u003C\u002Fa\u003Enotes, &#x201C;researchers have been using simple physical models of animals &#x2014; &#x2018;dummies&#x2019; &#x2014; to examine the social behavior of real animals, and biologists began animating their dummies as soon as technology would allow.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPhysicist Jos&#xE9; Halloy has been a pioneer in this area. One of his early efforts involved robots that could buddy up with, um, roaches.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"360\" width=\"480\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FkaU-ARCBO74?rel=0\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOK, OK, not very cute. But this was evidently a successful early example of a &#x201C;mixed aggregation society&#x201D; &#x2014; a demonstration that animals and machines could successfully mingle for the benefit of human study.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELater Halloy and roboticist Francesco Mondada embarked on an experiment involving a more charismatic subject: baby chicks.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EChicks are known to form a bond, or &#x201C;imprint,&#x201D; with &#x201C;nearly any moving object they encounter in the early hours of their lives,&#x201D; as \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnautil.us\u002Fissue\u002F10\u002Fmergers--acquisitions\u002Fanimals-bow-to-their-mechanical-overlords\"\u003Ethis Nautilus article\u003C\u002Fa\u003E put it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESo researchers came up with a color-lit, beep-emitting mobile gizmo, roughly the size of a mother hen &#x2014; PoulBot, it was evidently called. It worked with about 60 percent of its adorable little subjects.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Baby chicks with the PoulBot\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F0530f990ad7807f72a82514fe4ccb42fcc472799.png\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnautil.us\u002Fissue\u002F10\u002Fmergers--acquisitions\u002Fanimals-bow-to-their-mechanical-overlords\"\u003ENautilus\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EClearly the motivations for these efforts vary quite a bit &#x2014; some are about capturing images, but many are about finding new ways to gather other forms of data. But all turn on the idea of using machines to replace the problem-filled strategy of a disruptive human barging onto the scene.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOf course, all of this could turn out to be bad news if the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Felon-musk-warns-against-developing-artificial-101086558879.html\"\u003Eartificial-intelligence fears of Elon Musk and the like\u003C\u002Fa\u003E come true &#x2014; will animals side against us in the great robot wars of the future?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMaybe. Wondering why, Marucci began researching sensors and accelerometers, most suited for use in helmets or even do-rags.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"The Solution to Football Concussions May Come from This &#x2018;Smartphone in Your Mouth&#x2019;\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fe3f36faa169e76c0eab1cd1e017b18573f139703.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(\u003Cspan\u003EJohn Ballance\u002F\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftheadvocate.com\u002F\"\u003EThe Advocate\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E  \n\u003Cp\u003EJack Marucci is the director of athletic training at LSU, where the nationally ranked football team averages about six concussions during a month of training camp, but only two or three during a season spanning from September until January.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EUsually, the concussions are suffered by the largest men on the field, the offensive and defensive linemen.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWondering why, Marucci began researching sensors and accelerometers most suited for use in helmets or even do-rags.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ENothing was quite right until he stumbled across&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.i1biometrics.com\u002F\"\u003Ei1 Biometrics&#x2019; Vector MouthGuard\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which addressed his questions and concerns differently &#x2014; its sensors are embedded inside the age-old protective dental device, delivering a more accurate and real-time measure of force to the head.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s a fixed portion of your skull,&#x201D; explains Jesse Harper, i1 Biometrics&#x2019; CEO. &#x201C;Think of it like a smartphone in your mouth. We have accelerometers, gyroscopes, microprocessors &#x2014; all of those things in the mouthguard.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;So, because of the fit with your teeth, everywhere your skull goes, the mouthguard is able to measure that.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAdds Marucci: &#x201C;It was a perfect marriage of what we were looking for &#x2014; more data &#x2026; It&#x2019;s like having a computer on board. It can check for safety. It&#x2019;s basically another set of eyes you can have.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe results are transmitted to a trainer or physician on the sideline, viewable via laptop or smartphone. There are no lights or buttons &#x2014; once the mouthpiece is inserted, it turns on. It comes with a clamshell charging case that runs on a pair of AA batteries that should last an entire season.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMade from ExxonMobil&#x2019;s Vistamaxx elastic polymer technology, the Vector MouthGuard is extremely durable, which is key because the cost &#x2014; $199 &#x2014; might be prohibitive for some, particularly high-school players.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ficdn6.digitaltrends.com\u002Fimage\u002Fi1-biometrics-vector-mouthguard-014-1500x1000.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"i1-Biometrics-Vector-MouthGuard-014\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F25d4f5f255ab11b2e2e5e5d0025f703661dccc99.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n\u003Cem\u003E(John Ballance\u002F\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\n\u003Cem\u003EThe Advocate)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHarper says the mouthpiece, which was field-tested this year by four high-school teams across the country and will be available for purchase at the start of the 2015 season, is designed for use in multiple sports. There will be an adult and a youth version.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s important to note that this product will not diagnose concussions, the hot-button topic surrounding football (and athletics, really) at all levels. But the information gathered from the Vector MouthGuard can lead to increased detection and awareness.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWho isn&#x2019;t interested in that?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Yes, we&#x2019;re for-profit, but I got into this because I care about the sport,&#x201D; Harper says. &#x201C;I want to keep these players as safe as possible, have a better understanding of what they&#x2019;re going through on the field of play, coach them and give them better tools to be successful and ultimately help the sport &#x2026; The NFL does things like move the kickoffs forward for less acceleration time. We don&#x2019;t know if that does anything. If we have a different helmet type, does that translate to force to the head? Playing on grass or turf? Three-point stance versus two-point stance? &#x2026;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E&#x201C;This is the first scalable way to get this data from these players, to build context. That&#x2019;s my ultimate goal.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAlready, it has served as a vital teaching tool at LSU.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere is a secondary benefit as well. Because areas of impact can be traced &#x2014; a 3D rendering of the head is among the data instantly transmitted &#x2014; it can also serve as a performance device. If a player is ducking his head during a tackle and using the crown of his helmet, which is not only an enforceable penalty but also dangerous, potentially career-threatening, it can be fixed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It has already corrected some of our guys,&#x201D; Marucci says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHe estimates that 20 players are currently using the Vector MouthGuard, down from an original 30, a dip the athletic trainer attributes to &#x201C;compliance.&#x201D; It seems some simply don&#x2019;t want to use the high-tech mouthpiece.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut the data culled from those who stuck with it? It has reinforced Marucci&#x2019;s theories, particularly regarding the offensive and defensive linemen, those behemoths most apt to sustain concussions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ficdn2.digitaltrends.com\u002Fimage\u002Fi1-biometrics-vector-mouthguard-012-1500x1000.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"i1-Biometrics-Vector-MouthGuard-012\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F0e6fed3b925ea66721ae6db9f01db5470a8eaa07.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(John Ballance\u002F\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cem\u003EThe Advocate)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s micro-traumas,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;A lot of contact. They&#x2019;re always making contact. People don&#x2019;t look at that as much. They see the big blow and the guy goes down &#x2026; This gave us confirmation on an offensive lineman in a regular practice may take &#x2014; the cut-off for an &#x2018;impact&#x2019; hit is 25&#xA0;Gs or greater &#x2013; up to 15 to 20 &#x2018;impacts&#x2019; a practice.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Over a year, if you add this up, it gives us some relevance to say we need Earlier this year, HBO announced that it would launch a standalone streaming service in 2015, and now competitor Showtime has followed suit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe acclaimed channel currently hosts popular shows such as \u003Cem\u003EMasters of Sex, Penny Dreadful,\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem\u003EShameless,\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and previously played host to offbeat fan favorites like \u003Cem\u003EThe Borgias, The L Word,\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem\u003EWeeds.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E It also costs a pretty penny: Providers like Comcast and DirecTV often charge anywhere between $10 and $15 per month for Showtime on top of an existing cable package.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMORE:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.tomsguide.com\u002Fus\u002Fbest-streaming-players,review-2140.html\"\u003EBest Streaming Players: Chromecast, Roku, Apple TV &amp; More\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDuring a CBS third quarter financial results meeting (CBS owns Showtime), chief executive officer Leslie Moonves discussed Showtime at length. He explained that Showtime was responsible for a large part of the company&#x2019;s 2 percent revenue increase. In order to capitalize on Showtime&#x2019;s popularity, CBS will introduce an online streaming service for Showtime programs sometime in 2015.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhether the service will be subscription or &#xE0; la carte, when it will launch, and how much it will cost are all still up in the air. However, it will be a standalone service &#x2014; no preexisting cable package required. As it stands, users can indeed stream Showtime series with their computers, mobile devices, and set-top boxes, but doing so requires a cable subscription with a Showtime package.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIf HBO and Showtime inspire a large number of videophiles to finally cut the cord and live with streaming services instead of cable subscriptions, expect other premium channels to follow suit. Band: Beautiful … on the Inside","summary":"Microsoft’s new $200 Fitness Band ($200) doesn’t just have one sensor inside — it has 10. Including GPS. It's an incredibly capable health monitoring device, and a good smartwatch, too. David Pogue reviews.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EMillions of people are slipping fitness bands onto their wrists these days, and that&#x2019;s great. Anything that can get our overfed, underslept population moving more and sleeping better is a welcome invention.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut these are motivational instruments, not scientific ones.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhat&#x2019;s in most fitness bands from&#xA0;UP, Nike, and Fitbit&#xA0;are accelerometers &#x2014; tilt sensors, glorified pedometers. They give you insight into how many steps you take each day and what portion of the night you toss and turn, but that&#x2019;s about it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMicrosoft&#x2019;s new Band ($200) is a different story. This thing doesn&#x2019;t just have one sensor inside &#x2014; it has&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003E10.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Band: Beautiful &#x2026; on the Inside\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w451\u002F80593f2ce91be48f31475bdc1c590fd7acd0949d.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt measures ultraviolet light, so you have some warning before you head out without sunscreen. It can measure skin temperature. It can even measure stress (with a galvanic skin sensor).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt has GPS&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Ebuilt in\u003C\u002Fem\u003E &#x2014; also a first for a wristband this size. If you&#x2019;re a runner, that could be a deal-maker: It means you don&#x2019;t have to carry your phone to track your run. Once the device has a chance to connect with your smartphone, its app shows you a map of your route, color coded to your speed, with mile markers. It&#x2019;s great information.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Run tracker\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fbbc21b8b436f789985335085c7e808c17cee1d03.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EFinally, the Band measures your heart rate continuously.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMonitoring your pulse multiplies the usefulness of a band. For one thing, it makes the plotting of your sleep cycles far more accurate, because it can tell when your&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Emetabolism&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fem\u003Eis slowing down, not just when your wrist has stopped moving. For another, resting heart rate is an important general health statistic. Runners and other athletes also like to know how close they are to their maximum heart rates.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Step-counter\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Facf42152e648b4a80b46e651f2c47201f8069167.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe smartwatch\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EOn top of all that, the Microsoft Band is a smartwatch. Its bright, crisp, sunlight-readable touchscreen shows text messages, email, phone calls (name and number), Facebook and Twitter posts, and other notifications from your phone. A subtle vibration on your wrist tells you there&#x2019;s something to look at.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Band\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Ff812b628f4694b0c333ffe964b69a07374dd9183.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Microsoft Band&#x2019;s design bears some resemblance to Samsung&#x2019;s&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Feverybody-talks-about-self-driving-cars-and-flying-84362915699.html\"\u003EGear Fit\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. But there are big differences.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOne is that Microsoft &#x2014; Microsoft! &#x2014; is making its health initiative as open as possible. The other big players lock you into their product lines. Apple&#x2019;s watch will require an iPhone. Samsung&#x2019;s watches require Samsung phones.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut the app for Microsoft&#x2019;s band is available for iPhones, Android phones,&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Eand&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fem\u003EWindows Phones.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYour fitness data isn&#x2019;t locked into that Microsoft app, either. Already, you can share its data with popular apps from other companies, like MapMyFitness, RunKeeper, and MyFitnessPal.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn fact, Microsoft says its ultimate goal is for its Band and its companion Health app to work with&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Eeverything out there.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fem\u003EEven Apple&#x2019;s Health app and Google&#x2019;s Fit app. &#x201C;We&#x2019;ll have more to share on that soon,&#x201D; the company says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThat&#x2019;s an incredibly customer-friendly, smart, and refreshing move. OK, Microsoft: Who are you and what have you done with the world&#x2019;s biggest software company?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMicrosoft&#x2019;s smartwatch implementation is slick, polished, and unobtrusive. You have control over which kinds of things make your wrist buzz, and you never get lost. If you have Android or a Windows Phone, you can respond to text messages with canned responses. If you have a Windows Phone, you can even dictate notes and reminders to your phone with your voice.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYour calendar can show up here. There&#x2019;s even a Starbucks &#x201C;tile&#x201D; among the options. With a touch, it displays the barcode from a Starbucks card, so you can pay for your coffee without having to bring your wallet&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Eor\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&#xA0;your phone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Band showing weather, meeting, and UV sensor\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w442\u002F8a93449edca4f82b0697a4d0b35dd587bb752cc7.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMicrosoft says you can wear the Band either on the inside or outside of your wrist. I found that it works best on the inside. There it&#x2019;s more comfortable &#x2014; and if you&#x2019;re with other people, you can take sly peeks at incoming messages without awkwardly pulling out your phone or looking at the back of your wrist.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe app\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EThe software design &#x2014; both on the watch and the phone &#x2014; is clean, readable, and easy to figure out. On the watch, for example, you swipe across the screen to view the different functions, and tap one to trigger it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Band\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F33db0b1e2caebd9ec1cb3669fa0ee7a80329b532.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhich &#x201C;tiles&#x201D; appear here, and in which order, is up to you. The app lets you set everything up:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Band organization screen\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F3a371c992ed37a725fa921d94b53bff3104f5ee7.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe app is easy to navigate, too. You tap a tile to expand it and review its data.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe only problem is that there&#x2019;s not&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Eenough&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fem\u003Eof the app. For example, the Sleep graph is extremely informative &#x2014;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Sleep graph on Microsoft Band\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F61fdf9ee8c4a9a08f84499ef6e1292d7e77805c3.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x2014; but there&#x2019;s no way to see any&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Epast\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&#xA0;nights&#x2019; sleep. It&#x2019;d be nice to see a graph of your sleep over the past week or month, for example. Or to turn the phone 90 degrees for a wider graph.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESimilarly, you know the stress and skin-temperature sensors? Guess where their data shows up? Nowhere. Not on the phone, not on the watch. (Coming soon, Microsoft says.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe UV light sensor is very cool &#x2014; another first on a general fitness band (see also the&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fthe-netatmo-june-an-elegant-uv-detector-that-could-be-89365997539.html\"\u003ENetatmo June\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Tap its icon on the watch, point it at the sky, and it tells you, for example: &#x201C;Typical time to sunburn: 60 minutes.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut this data never makes it back to the app. There&#x2019;s no record of it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMicrosoft says that two huge Band\u002FHealth components are coming in December. First, a website where you&#x2019;ll be able to slice and dice your health data in more flexible ways.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESecond, insights that analyze all that fitness data, and even take into account what&#x2019;s on your calendar. It will tell you, for example, &#x201C;Your heart rate spiked the last two times you met with your editor.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EJawbone&#x2019;s UP band already takes small steps toward teasing useful conclusions out of your data. But there are miles to go; this sort of analysis is the screamingly obvious next step for personal fitness trackers. We don&#x2019;t need data; we need knowledge.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe workout\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EHere&#x2019;s something else nobody else&#x2019;s band does: guides you through workouts.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the Microsoft Health app, you look over a menu of free workouts from various fitness companies:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Health app\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fbf87e65adb44fe8b21e501bad7b23414035a262b.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOn the phone, you preview the phases of the workout; some even offer videos that show you the correct technique. With one tap, you send that workout to your band.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThen, in the gym or on the track, the watch guides you through the workout. It counts the reps, vibrates when it&#x2019;s time for the next exercise, and tracks your time and heart rate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Band showing workout instructions\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F6823c06561f6e6ef9c546f4cf30c84fd6559bfce.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the phone app, you get a tally of calories burned and an estimate of your muscles&#x2019; recovery time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis guided-workout feature truly works. Knowing that there&#x2019;s some entity in charge, even if it&#x2019;s a blob of software, somehow makes it easier to stick to a plan and get the workout done.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe band\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EYou&#x2019;re probably starting to guess already that this is one very sophisticated band. There is a&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Elot&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fem\u003Ebuilt into it:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Exploded view of Microsoft Band\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F7d4cf49d746cc089402a7f878cdbf639198c78cd.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere is, however, one serious Band failure &#x2014; and that&#x2019;s the actual band.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s thick, chunky, and made of hard rubber. The screen is a rigid, 2-inch slab that makes no attempt to curve with your wrist (unlike Samsung&#x2019;s Fit). In short, this band is neither stylish nor comfortable.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Band strap\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F9dfb0b377fdb152866cd4e7804401ef9ce236e51.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMost of the time, you can forget you&#x2019;re wearing it. But the Band can dig into your wrist when, for example, you&#x2019;re typing, or tucking your arm under a pillow at night. It snags any sleeve you try to pass over it. You definitely won&#x2019;t be seeing this band on anyone&#x2019;s arm at Fashion Week.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Band isn&#x2019;t waterproof, either. It&#x2019;ll handle splashes and handwashing, but you have to take it off to shower or swim. Rats.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMicrosoft says the battery generally lasts two days on a charge. To my surprise, I routinely got&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Ethree\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&#xA0;full days except when I ran with GPS turned on. That&#x2019;s a juice-guzzler.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe charging cable clicks onto the inside of the Band magnetically, from either side. It&#x2019;s a solid, satisfying design, but of course it&#x2019;s proprietary. It&#x2019;s not as convenient as the microUSB cables that come with most other gadgets these days.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI will say this for the design, though: The clasp is fantastic. It snaps quickly into place and is easily adjustable while on your wrist. The metal-prong-in-rubber-slot design of the other bands look Neanderthal by comparison.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Microsoft Band clasp\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w381\u002Ff83af5986bd4e321426f910f5122a70a357e1f2e.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe landscape\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EContinuous heart-rate monitoring is The New Thing in fitness trackers. Jawbone just announced a new band called the&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fjawbone-announces-more-stylish-more-functional-up3-and-101853384834.html\"\u003EUP3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;($180, not available yet). No screen, no smartwatch features &#x2014; but continuous heart tracking and seven-day battery life.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"UP3 fitness tracker\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F85a1acf76ad3f8780f0a3b088a45f3719e68e13b.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnd the new Basis Peak watch ($200) has many of the same advantages of the Microsoft Band (continuous heart-rate monitor, galvanic skin response, skin temperature, smartwatch notifications), plus it&#x2019;s waterproof. Then again, it&#x2019;s a watch, not a band &#x2014; and a honkin&#x2019; big one.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Basis Peak watch\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fe390ab821e4efbfd37ee9c74988d59336cfb52d1.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWe&#x2019;re at the dawn of the self-tracking movement. It&#x2019;s really a big deal. It could change or even save a lot of lives. It means that you can know yourself, learn things about yourself, every hour of every day, in ways that used to require a doctor&#x2019;s visit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut at this point, you can have either a thin, lovely band, or one stuffed with useful sensors. Not both.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMicrosoft, however, has struck the sweetest spot yet on that seesaw of compromise. Yes, the Band is chunky and industrial looking. But it&#x2019;s got more features for its size than any rival yet, and it does a lot of things no other gadget can. And the fact that Microsoft intends to make it as compatible as possible? That&#x2019;s going to be healthy both for Microsoft and for you.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EGet David Pogue&#x2019;s&#xA0;columns sent to&#xA0;you by email! e\u002Fjpeg","width":550,"height":315,"size_type":"550","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w600\u002F74f0d21bbe5bfc92c3b2151f30008feda5210528.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":600,"height":343,"size_type":"600","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w700\u002F74f0d21bbe5bfc92c3b2151f30008feda5210528.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":700,"height":400,"size_type":"700","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w800\u002F74f0d21bbe5bfc92c3b2151f30008feda5210528.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":800,"height":458,"size_type":"800","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w900\u002F74f0d21bbe5bfc92c3b2151f30008feda5210528.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":900,"height":515,"size_type":"900","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w1000\u002F74f0d21bbe5bfc92c3b2151f30008feda5210528.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":1000,"height":572,"size_type":"1000","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w1100\u002F74f0d21bbe5bfc92c3b2151f30008feda5210528.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":1100,"height":629,"size_type":"1100","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w1131\u002F74f0d21bbe5bfc92c3b2151f30008feda5210528.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":1131,"height":647,"size_type":"original","formats":{},"title":"Microsoft Band: Beautiful … on the called Echo that lets people stream music and search the Internet, as the company works to extend its reach into consumers&#x2019; digital lives.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EEcho is priced at $199, Amazon said on its website today. Members of Amazon&#x2019;s Prime fast-shipping program can purchase the gadget for $99 for a limited period. Last week, the Seattle-based online retailer unveiled a media-streaming device, the Fire TV Stick, which plugs into a TV set to let users browse video and music from Netflix, Pandora, and other content services.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Amazon&#x2019;s Newest Gadget Is Like a Siri Voice Assistant for Your Home\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F57f3fc5e49f38512bb80c7cf538e546013fa2dc7.png\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(Amazon)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAmazon introduced Echo with little fanfare, simply putting up a webpage about the device. In April, Amazon similarly unveiled Dash, a barcode scanner and image-recognition device. Dash also has speech-recognition capabilities, with people able to push a microphone button on the device, say &#x201C;chocolate chips&#x201D; or some other item, and have the products deposited into their online Amazon shopping cart.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMore from Bloomberg.com:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bloomberg.com\u002Fnews\u002F2014-11-06\u002Fnato-f-16-jets-intercept-russian-spy-plane-latvia-says.html?cmpid=yhoo.inline\"\u003ENATO F-16 Jets Intercept Russian Spy Plane, Latvia Says\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMany of the new devices are the result of work from Amazon&#x2019;s Lab126 facility in Silicon Valley. Amazon has made at least two acquisitions of speech-technology companies in recent years.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ECraig Berman, a spokesman for Amazon, didn&#x2019;t immediately return a request for comment.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMore from Bloomberg.com:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bloomberg.com\u002Fnews\u002F2014-11-05\u002Fthose-sunspots-approaching-earth-could-bring-blackouts.html?cmpid=yhoo.inline\"\u003EThose Sunspots Approaching Earth Could Bring Blackouts\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAmazon said on its website today that Echo works when a consumer speaks the word &#x201C;Alexa&#x201D; to wake the device up. The gadget is connected to the Web and runs on Amazon Web Services, the company&#x2019;s cloud-computing service. Over time, Echo can adjust to consumers&#x2019; speech patterns and personal preferences, Amazon said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EEcho faces competition from other providers of connected speakers, including Sonos and Jawbone. Jawbone offers a line of connected streaming home speakers called Jambox, in a range of colors and sizes costing $130 to $300. Sonos makes speakers starting at $199 that let people stream music from computers, mobile devices, and online services such as Pandora and Spotify.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESome of Amazon&#x2019;s hardware offerings have flopped in the past, and it&#x2019;s unclear whether the Echo will have mass appeal. Last month, Amazon reported a $170 million inventory charge for the third quarter related to excess supplies of its Fire smartphone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftopics.bloomberg.com\u002Fmichael-pachter\u002F?cmpid=yhoo.hlinks\"\u003EMichael Pachter\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, an analyst at Wedbush Securities in Los Angeles, said he doesn&#x2019;t understand why people might be tempted to purchase Echo.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I think it&#x2019;s just a two-way speaker, but why isn&#x2019;t there just an app that lets me do the same thing without having to spend $99 on hardware?&#x201D; he said. &#x201C;I think this is a solution that is seeking a problem.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E After that, the emergency crew on site instructed the worker how to fix the platform. Launches First-of-Its-Kind 24-Hour Streaming News Channel","summary":"CBS is today launching an online news channel that’ll be broadcasting over its website and apps 24 hours a day, all week long.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"CBS Launches First-of-Its-Kind 24-Hour Streaming News Channel\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fdbadd3c63f6d2e816f4884ac8585f3aa27f14d7a.png\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ECBS is today launching&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcbsn.cbsnews.com\u002F\"\u003Ean online news channel\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E&#xA0;that&#x2019;ll be broadcasting over its website and apps 24 hours a day, all week long. CBS is naming the new network&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcbsn.cbsnews.com\u002F\"\u003ECBSN\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, and it plans to fill it with live, anchored coverage from 9 a.m. to midnight Eastern every weekday. This is the first digital streaming news channel out there, according to CBS, and it&#x2019;s certainly an ambitious move on the network&#x2019;s part that shows it&#x2019;s taking the move toward online distribution seriously. Just last month, it also began&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2014\u002F10\u002F16\u002F6987543\u002Fcbs-all-access-streaming-service-no-cable-required-launches\"\u003Eoffering streaming access to CBS proper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E&#xA0;with a subscription.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ECBSN&#x2019;s content doesn&#x2019;t mirror what you&#x2019;ll find on CBS, offering its own coverage as well as content from CBS News, Sports, and other affiliates. The network says that it may also switch to showing CBS News content when breaking reports are being aired. But viewing the stream live is only one way to watch CBSN: It also allows viewers to skip around through prior coverage, almost in an on-demand style for recently aired segments. You&#x2019;ll be able to watch the network on CBS&#x2019;s website as well as on the Roku and Fire TV. It&#x2019;s also available on CBS News&#x2019; Windows 8 app, and it&#x2019;ll come to its Android app before the end of the year. CBS doesn&#x2019;t make note of whether access will be available on Apple&#x2019;s platforms.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E&#x201C;There&#x2019;s a tremendous opportunity on these platforms for a true round-the-clock newscast,&#x201D; CBS CEO Les Moonves said in a statement. &#x201C;We&#x2019;re confident this service will appeal to both traditional news consumers and a whole new set of viewers.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EThe service is supported by commercials, meaning that CBSN isn&#x2019;t all that different of a venture than what CBS is already used to. Moonves knows there are a good number of viewers out there who only want to watch TV online, and increasingly he&#x2019;s been willing to give it to them.
